<div id="review_1789892958" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1789892958" />
    <a title="Bibi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi"><img alt="Bibi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602128191p2/33411728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1789892958?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bibi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bibi" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi">Bibi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25566212-heartless">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1789892958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1852029542479000748"><blockquote>Arrrgggh... I can feel the knives being sharpened. *gulp* <br/><br/><b>So, can we talk about this book first before you send the knife my way?<br/><br/></b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18584855-heartless' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heartless</a> is an imagined prequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13023.Alice_in_Wonderland?ac=1&from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alice in Wonderland</a> but with its main focus being the "Queen of Hearts", she of the famous "Off with their heads" quote.<br/><br/><blockquote><a href='http://s1248.photobucket.com/user/bibifagboyegun/media/26926e15-1b5c-426b-8489-6b0e19db04fa_zpslsykouv3.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479168008i/21155711.png' alt=' photo 26926e15-1b5c-426b-8489-6b0e19db04fa_zpslsykouv3.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a></blockquote>
<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13023.Alice_in_Wonderland?ac=1&from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alice in Wonderland</a> is a fantastical story written in 1865 by Lewis Carrol, who created the glorious dystopian world of Wonderland replete with a talking cheshire cat, a bumbling rabbit, knaves, Jabberwocks and muc</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1852029542479000748" style="display:none"><blockquote>Arrrgggh... I can feel the knives being sharpened. *gulp* <br><br><b>So, can we talk about this book first before you send the knife my way?<br><br></b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18584855-heartless" rel="nofollow noopener">Heartless</a> is an imagined prequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13023.Alice_in_Wonderland?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice in Wonderland</a> but with its main focus being the "Queen of Hearts", she of the famous "Off with their heads" quote.<br><br><blockquote><a href="http://s1248.photobucket.com/user/bibifagboyegun/media/26926e15-1b5c-426b-8489-6b0e19db04fa_zpslsykouv3.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479168008i/21155711.png" alt=" photo 26926e15-1b5c-426b-8489-6b0e19db04fa_zpslsykouv3.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></blockquote>
<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13023.Alice_in_Wonderland?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice in Wonderland</a> is a fantastical story written in 1865 by Lewis Carrol, who created the glorious dystopian world of Wonderland replete with a talking cheshire cat, a bumbling rabbit, knaves, Jabberwocks and much more. I truly liked and enjoyed Alice in Wonderland; the book and the movie.<br><br>As this is my first Meyer book, I went into this with zero bias but with an expectation of getting, at the least, a fabulous intro to this best-selling author's work and at most, a thrilling account of the QOH's descent into madness. And yes, there is a good reason. A very tragic one, in fact. <br><br><b>So, who was the QOH? The book blurb -below- does a spiffing job of summarizing the story perfectly. Emphasis by me.</b><br><br><blockquote>Long before she was the terror of Wonderland—the infamous Queen of Hearts—<u><i>she was just a girl who wanted to fall in love</i></u><br><br><u><i>Catherine may be one of the most desired girls in Wonderland</i></u> and a favorite of the unmarried King of Hearts, but her interests lie elsewhere. <u><i>A talented baker</i></u>, all she wants is to open a shop with her best friend.....<br><br>Then Cath meets Jest, the handsome and mysterious court joker.......... <u><i>she and Jest enter into an intense, secret courtship</i></u>. Cath is determined to define her own destiny and fall in love on her terms. <u><i>But in a land thriving with magic, madness, and monsters, fate has other plans.</i></u>
</blockquote>
<br>Let's talk about the parts that were underlined. <br><br><b>One.</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Catherine didn't strike me as one who wanted to fall in love, I do believe she showed more passion for her macaroons and pies than for anyone or anything else, IMO. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><b>Two.</b> Desired by whom? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There were zero eligible men in Hearts and her lone suitor was the vapid King of Hearts. Moreover, aside from her baking talents, there was nothing special about her. Yes, we were told she was quite beautiful but seeing this is a land filled more with creatures than damsels, we had no point of reference for her implied beauty. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><b>Three.</b> Gosh, I'd never wanted a pie so badly. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Catherine was the consummate baker and really, the best part of this story is the baking. I gained inches just reading about the pies and the cakes and the macaroons. <i>*frantically searching my kitchen for any baked goods*</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> So, yes, mad props to Catherine for her baking skills.<br><br><b>Four.</b> Jest. The mysterious Joker who mesmerizes Cath, both with his talent and his beauty. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Here's where I think the story became undone. With Catherine being the daughter of a Marquess, any relationship with Jest the commoner would have been completely forbidden. <b>Pause here.</b> Remember Romeo and Juliet (or insert your favorite forbidden love story)? The angst? The late night trysts? The completely OTT love fest? How your heart ached for the lovers and how you cursed the Capulet and Montague feud? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Meyer had taken enough literary liberties with this story and could have done so much more with Jest. So much more. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Instead, I found him bland, boring, cloying, and unremarkable, despite his yellow eyes and the magic. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <b>Their love was supposedly forbidden therefore I expected frothing emotions and escalating tensions. I wanted to feel that heart-pounding despair evoked by young and desperate lovers who could not exist without the other.</b> <br><br>Had Meyer not spent more time invoking the spirit of the original AIW, had she not included any and every character from that book, Jest and Catherine may have had more time together building their longing for each other. Between the croquet matches; the uninteresting balls; Catherine's never-will-happen dream of opening a bakery; and the detailed descriptions of the aforementioned endless list of creatures; these two had less than 5 intimate moments. 5! In a book with 450+ pages!<br><br>Of the 450+pages, nearly 360 pages were nothing more than a retelling of the original AIW, the story only picks up momentum at the 80% mark but by which point,<blockquote><b>I. WAS. FRIGGING. BORED. OUT. OF. MY. MIND.</b></blockquote>
<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So, yes, Catherine witnesses a horrific incident which sends her careening into a pool of despair culminating in unreserved anger toward every single person she ever loved. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And thus, we finally are gifted with the whys of her apparent madness. Ultimately, Meyer does serve up a plausible accounting of the Queen's descent into madness, but like I said, during the entire journey to that conclusion: <blockquote><b>I. WAS. FRIGGING. BORED. OUT. OF. MY. FRIGGING. MIND.</b></blockquote>
<br>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1852029542479000748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1499783627" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1499783627" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1499783627?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melanie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4127670-mary">Mary</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=subscription-box-owlcrate">subscription-box-owlcrate</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1499783627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9521444933580500886"><i>Heartless</i> blew me away. If you've been following my reviews for a while, you will know that I wasn't the biggest fan of <i>The Lunar Chronicles</i>. Yes, I know, I can barely believe it either. So, I went into this book not expecting much, and maybe that helped, because this book blew me away. It surpassed every expectation I set for a five star book, and it was nothing short of perfection.<br/><br/>Also, regarding <i>The Lunar Chronicles</i>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1494277256' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fairest</a> was my favorite installment in that series, and the book I gave the </span>
  <span id="freeText9521444933580500886" style="display:none"><i>Heartless</i> blew me away. If you've been following my reviews for a while, you will know that I wasn't the biggest fan of <i>The Lunar Chronicles</i>. Yes, I know, I can barely believe it either. So, I went into this book not expecting much, and maybe that helped, because this book blew me away. It surpassed every expectation I set for a five star book, and it was nothing short of perfection.<br><br>Also, regarding <i>The Lunar Chronicles</i>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1494277256" rel="nofollow noopener">Fairest</a> was my favorite installment in that series, and the book I gave the highest rating. So, maybe I just really enjoy "villain" retellings? I think both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1494277256" rel="nofollow noopener">Fairest</a> and <i>Heartless</i> just speak to my tragic love-story masochist heart or something along those lines.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Two Rooks, a Pawn, and a Queen. That’s how the riddle begins, but howsoever shall it end?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Anyway, <i>Heartless</i> is a <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> retelling, that stars the Queen of Hearts before she was the Queen of Hearts. We have grown up reading about the evil queen and the evil things that she has done, but we never knew why she was the way she was. Well, bless Marissa Meyer for creating this heartfelt masterpiece, because she did just that. <br><br>The Queen of Hearts, known as Catherine in this story, was once not evil at all. In fact, she was quite the opposite and had dreams of opening up her own bakery, because she is the best baker in all of Hearts, and loves nothing more than to make people happy with her treats. <br><br>That is, until Catherine realizes that her parents expect her to marry the King of Hearts, and give up her dreams, that they deem unworthy, completely. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“If I am not to have happiness, let me at least have a purpose. Let me give you the heart of a queen.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I believe this is the main moral of this story, and what made this story resonate so much inside of me: You shouldn't live your life for anyone's expectations of you. Not your family, not your partner, not your friends, no one but yourself. No matter if we are in Wonderland or in our world, we are only allotted a certain amount of time, so spend your time doing what you love and what your heart tells you to do. I know I sound preachy, and I know this seems like a basic concept, but this is something I've struggled with my whole life and I know there are others out there that do too. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Sometimes your heart is the only thing worth listening to.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The Queen of Hearts isn't the only origin story for this book; we also learn a great deal about the Mad Hatter, and what was the final straw to make him truly mad. This plot reveal/twist was probably my favorite thing of this entire book, and it, along with Catherine's madness, made so much sense to me. Hatta's confession rebroke my heart all over again, honestly. <br><br>I knew how this story would end, obviously, but that didn't prepare me for how obsessed I would become trying to learn how we'd get to that ending. I kept trying to figure it out, and even though I guessed "the who", I never guessed "the how". I'm a terrible sucker for prophecy stories, but even reading the prophecy itself didn't prepare me for what actually happened. I felt gutted, heartbroken, and was completely unprepared. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It is a dangerous thing to unbelieve something only because it frightens you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>When I was a young girl, I would spend countless hours on my Grandparent's property, in all their different gardens, playing <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> with my Grandma. <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> started my obsession with finding "magical doorways" and, to this day, I still love reading about them. I also feel like a major reason I enjoyed this book is because it made me feel a lot of nostalgia to the point that I actually want to reread and rewatch different <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> adaptations. I am so blessed and thankful for those memories with my Grandma, and all the feelings attached to those memories. Those feelings really made me enjoy the reading experience even more, even though I know it made me a little biased. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476784596ra/20879675.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was the perfect amount of magical, beautiful and heartbreaking. It is written so lyrically, I feel like I highlighted half of the book. I loved it, and I love that it surprised me by loving it. I also love that it is a standalone. This is such a fantastic read, and I really can't recommend it enough, especially if you are like me and didn't love <i>The Lunar Chronicles</i>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Off with his head.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Also, now I'm just being overly emotional and tearing up, because I just noticed that the naked back cover has a joker hat. Before, I only noticed the front had the queen's crown. Please, my heart. This story will haunt me for some time, and I will never read <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> the same way. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Over everything, I choose you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9521444933580500886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1410567780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1410567780" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1410567780?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1410567780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13241367853827808211"><b>4.5<br/><br/>"She would not allow fate to trick her out of this dream."</b><br/><br/>I <i>almost</i> didn't read this. I thought, Oh well, another retelling. It can wait. I've got more promising things to read at the moment. But when I saw how <b>stunning</b> this <b>hardback </b>was, the shallower half of me immediately decided she had to read it like yesterday.<br/>Have I mentioned how much I love Shallow-Me?<br/><br/>•First of all, I think Marissa Meyer showed great wisdom in the choice of the story. Retelling <b>the Queen of Hearts</b> gave her the possibil</span>
  <span id="freeText13241367853827808211" style="display:none"><b>4.5<br /><br />"She would not allow fate to trick her out of this dream."</b><br /><br />I <i>almost</i> didn't read this. I thought, Oh well, another retelling. It can wait. I've got more promising things to read at the moment. But when I saw how <b>stunning</b> this <b>hardback </b>was, the shallower half of me immediately decided she had to read it like yesterday.<br />Have I mentioned how much I love Shallow-Me?<br /><br />•First of all, I think Marissa Meyer showed great wisdom in the choice of the story. Retelling <b>the Queen of Hearts</b> gave her the possibility to create something that was close enough to <i>The Lunar Chronicles</i> to please her historical fans, and different enough to let them see that the two things are unmistakably<i> not</i> alike. <i>Heartless</i> is <b>darker</b>, <b>gloomier</b>, and far, far <b>sadder</b> than any book of <i>The Lunar Chronicles</i> ever was, and, as much as I adore <i>The Lunar Chronicles</i>, I daresay this pinch of sorrow is precisely what made me fall, fall and fall for Catherine's story. <br /><br />•The true strong suit of the novel, if you ask me, is Catherine's change throughout it. I am not even sure I can properly call it "development", given the positive connotation this word usually comes with, but our heroine does grow, in a broad sense: she gets <b>stronger</b>,<b> tougher</b>, <b>less pliant</b>, <b>more tenacious</b>. Hers is <b>a growth that goes in so many directions</b> that it becomes impossible not only to label it simply as a descent into madness, but also to determine which parts of it can be considered an improvement and which cannot. Catherine's character expands while shrinking, learns to stand her ground while letting go, opens her eyes in the very same moment when what her world requires of her is to shut them as tight as she can. She's <b>contradictory</b>, <b>ensnared</b>, <b>caught in the crossfire</b>, and she has no one to blame for it.<br />Or rather, she has herself. <br />But she is tender, she is delicate; she cannot live with such a guilt. And that's where her torment stems from in the first place.<br />You wouldn't believe the transformation she undergoes from the beginning of the book to its end, truly. But in this, she never changes. <b>She never learns to shoulder this particular responsibility</b>, and she keeps finding ways around it. <b>She wants, wants, wants so desperately</b>, but ultimately she chooses daydream over reality. She hopes, hopes, hopes, but never finds it in herself to act. Even<b> revenge</b>, for her, is a way to lay the blame elsewhere and relieve herself of it, so that she can pretend to be fine after all. <b>She never faces what happened</b>, not really. She chases this illusion until the very end, in her decision of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[getting rid of her heart <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br />A heroine would have fought.<br /> <b>But Catherine is no heroine</b>.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Mind my words, Cheshire, I will have you banished from this kingdom if you tempt me."<br />"An empty threat from an empty girl."<br /> She rounded on him, teeth flashing. "I am not empty. I am full to the brim with murder and revenge. I am overflowing and I do not think you wish for me to overflow on to you."<br />"There was a time" – Cheshire yawned – "when you overflowed with whimsy and icing sugar. I liked that Catherine better."</b>
</i><br /><br /><b>I absolutely, utterly, completely adore her</b>. And her character development, above all. I may be biased because <b>cold, heartless, ruthless female leads</b> automatically mean I'm sold. Even if they show up only for the last five chapters or so. <br /><br />•<b>Cath's relationship with her parents</b> is <b>heart-rending</b>. Every single time they talked to her, a part of me screamed and died in agony. Their last encounter brought real tears to my eyes. <b>Not being listened to</b>, not being <i>truly</i> considered by the two people who should be the most supportive and caring for you, that's a torture I wouldn't wish on the worst of my enemies. The Marquess and the Marchioness are probably the main reason why my very soul was in <b>agony</b> throughout the whole book.<br /><br />•On the other hand, there are <b>a couple of flaws</b> I couldn't help noticing (and forgetting, apparently. I was too caught up to take notes). I remember thinking that Cath's bitterness, after <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mary Ann's betrayal <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, seemed somewhat <b>too sudden</b>, and that it didn't seem to bode well for the character development, but as you can guess, my fears were unfounded, though the episode was indeed handled rather awkwardly, narratively speaking -she's like rainbow and sunshine one scene and storm and thunder the next. So, when you get there, don't panic: it's all but short-lived.<br /><br />•Another moment I would have written differently is when she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[decides to accept the King so as to allow Jest to accomplish his mission <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Again, it was kind of rushed and, I think, not very sensible, and that's probably the part of the book I like the least, but not so much that I couldn't turn a blind eye and keep enjoying the rest. <br /><br />•I'm not sure I fully grasped the meaning of the fact that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[some of Cath's dreams actually came true, like the lemon tree or the roses or the key lime <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I feel like I understand it on a subconscious level while not being able to put it in words. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maybe it was Fate -the Sisters- sending her messages? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I think I'll stick to this explanation.<br /><br />•I am just now realizing that I haven't mentioned <b>the romance</b> yet. <b>Jest</b> is an adorable love interest, and the ship sailed in no time, but <b>the point is, the romance in itself is not the point</b>. What actually is important is what this first love story means to Cath and how it would affect her life. This is why I wouldn't call Jest a male lead: <b>the only lead, here, is Catherine</b>. And I'm particularly happy with this. <br /><br />➽ I did not expect to enjoy <i>Heartless</i> as much as I did. <b>I did not expect to warm up so much to this girl in the habit of dreaming too much</b>, for whom hoping is an illness, for whom burying her hands in a ball of dough is the ultimate happiness. I warmed up to her so much my heart had got as cold as hers as the conclusion drew near, and by the end of it, it didn't even seem to be beating anymore. <br />I wonder if I will ever be able to claim it back.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13241367853827808211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1915408511?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mxa ☂︎" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mxa ☂︎" href="/user/show/36873117-mxa">mxa ☂︎</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781509814138" href="/book/show/31458203-heartless">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=babes-favs">babes-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1915408511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2117548482733808362">5 Red Roses<br/><br/><i>"A finely crafted hat makes a person ... bolder."</i><br/><br/>This is my first novel from Marissa Meyer and I have to say that I'm very happy with what I got. I pretty much went into it with no expectation. I only knew that it's somehow a retelling of Alice in Wonderland but really, it's the villain's story before she became the notorious Queen of Hearts and that was intriguing enough for me. Yet, Meyer managed to fill it up with a beautiful and fast-paced story that I was hooked from start to end</span>
  <span id="freeText2117548482733808362" style="display:none">5 Red Roses<br /><br /><i>"A finely crafted hat makes a person ... bolder."</i><br /><br />This is my first novel from Marissa Meyer and I have to say that I'm very happy with what I got. I pretty much went into it with no expectation. I only knew that it's somehow a retelling of Alice in Wonderland but really, it's the villain's story before she became the notorious Queen of Hearts and that was intriguing enough for me. Yet, Meyer managed to fill it up with a beautiful and fast-paced story that I was hooked from start to end.<br /><br />Heartless tells the story of a girl named Catherine, who's the daughter of a royal family going by Rock Turtle Cove in the Kingdom of Hearts. She is deemed to become the Queen as she is pressured by her parents (mostly by her mother, the Marchioness) to marry the very-available and ever giggling King. However, her passionate lies elsewhere and that's in her baking. For years, Catherine and her maid + best friend, Mary Ann, had dreams of opening up a bakery but it's of no use in a place where women are not supposed to be seen as "businessmen". <br />This tale continues with Catherine fighting for what she wants despite so many obstacles. But we all know how this story turns out in the end... Will she take risks and get the bakery of her dreams or lose everything she's worked so hard for to only be crowned as the Queen of Hearts?<br /><br /><i>Her mother sneered. "Then you are a fool."<br />"Good. I've become rather fond of fools."</i><br /><br />But that's not all, Heartless also introduces us to Jest, who is the King's court joker and Catherine's love-interest. I don't want to go into too much details but Jest has very own story that's definitely worth picking up this book for as <b>YOU SURELY DON'T WANT TO MISS OUT.</b> To those who have knowledge of Alice in Wonderland will also recognize side characters like Chesire, the White Rabbit, Mr. Caterpillar and so on.<br /><br /> <i>"Do you know you're extra beautiful when you talk about baking. You know you're good at it, and that knowledge lights you up."</i><br /><br />I chose to pick up Heartless for some light and fluffy read but <b>BOY WAS I WRONG.</b> The last 200+ pages was <b>SUPER INTENSE</b>, it was hard to put it down when I needed to. That still doesn't take away the fact that it wasn't funny throughout cause it actually was... the dessert references were on point that <b>I yearn for a bite all the damn time (especially the rose macarons)</b>, Catherine's fierceness, sassy Cheshire and of course, the flirtatious Joker but we also have Raven, Hatter, and many more lovable characters.<br /><br />I loved reading how realistic the characters in Heartless were in its traditional and magical sense. I was so not expecting that. For one, there's no denying that Catherine is flawed. She's short of shy and well-mannered but at the same time she tends to react very quickly. True to her manners, a lot of the times her mind wanders to sacrificing her own happiness for her family's wishes and to keep her reputation intact but still, she is determined to fight back. <br />Jest, on the other hand... gosh there are just no words to describe how <b>AMAZING</b> and <b>BEAUTIFUL</b> he is. How he treated Catherine throughout this entire book is <i>swoon-worthy</i> and I'm glad that their relationship wasn't instant as it may seems. The romance in this book you guys was <b>NOT</b> overwhelming. <br /><br /><i>"What are you doing here?" she whispered. "You're..."<br />He grinned. "A wanted man?"<br />She ducked beneath the raised hands of the next couple. Rotated back. Curtsied.<br />"Exactly," she said as her palm found Jest's again.<br />"Good," he said, his dimples showing. "I hoped you might still feel that way."</i><br /><br /><b>I HIGHLY RECOMMEND THIS BOOK TO EVERY ONE :D</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2117548482733808362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1565245365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1565245365" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1565245365?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1565245365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12673763468886531446"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>They were all a little mad, if one was to be forthright.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>BUDDY READ WITH SUNNY, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1680171507?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>MY FAVORITE CHILD</a>.<br/><br/>Okay so, <b>it's a big surprise I enjoyed this</b>. I knew I would simply because it's Marissa Meyer and she did not disappoint me with her Lunar Chronicles series, so I knew this would happen. Marissa is the only author that is able to write novels that captivate me from the very first sentence. To be honest, <b>I dislike retellings a lot.</b> I won't say I hate them, but we aren't very good friends. </span>
  <span id="freeText12673763468886531446" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>They were all a little mad, if one was to be forthright.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />BUDDY READ WITH SUNNY, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1680171507?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">MY FAVORITE CHILD</a>.<br /><br />Okay so, <b>it's a big surprise I enjoyed this</b>. I knew I would simply because it's Marissa Meyer and she did not disappoint me with her Lunar Chronicles series, so I knew this would happen. Marissa is the only author that is able to write novels that captivate me from the very first sentence. To be honest, <b>I dislike retellings a lot.</b> I won't say I hate them, but we aren't very good friends. Every retelling I read (or try to read) ends up unfinished or rated lowly. Marissa Meyer had me intrigued since the very beginning and I couldn't be happier. Heartless was <b>happy and cute, but it was also heartbreaking and now I am</b> <i>heartless?</i> I would say that's the word since I don't even know what my hearts for now.<br /><br /><i>Heartless</i> is a well-done and well-written retelling of Alice in Wonderland. I've also never been the biggest fan of Alice in Wonderland, so I was a little afraid going into this one when Sana asked me if I wanted to BR it with her. I said yes because I kinda thought she and I would think the same about it and well, I was glad, and I couldn't be happier of us Sana. Our buddy read finally worked! The Queen of Hearts was actually one of my favorite characters only because she was a bitch and had a rude attitude. Call me a bitch as well, but I liked her personality. For some reason, I did, but mainly because she's the Queen of Hearts that everyone else despised while I enjoyed her. <br /><br />Before becoming the rude Queen, <b>Catherine 'Cath' Pinkerton was just a normal girl who wanted to be happy by opening her own bakery with one of her good friends, Mary-Ann, and she wanted to fall in love, to be happy, to know what's it like to be in love.</b> Before turning into the Queen of Hearts and marrying the infamous King of Hearts, Cath just wanted her own fairytale of falling in love and feeling passion, to be happy while she lived the young life she had. Her parents, being the strict parents that don't really care what happiness for their daughter is and what it really means, don't want her to do that and don't approve of it. Instead, they try pushing her into becoming the only girl that can be seen at a royal ball where the King himself can fall in love with her and propose to her, and that is exactly what happens. The King of Hearts, <b>an immature and childish boy who does not have the capability of ruling a kingdom, proposes to Catherine.</b> He does not show any love and affection towards her in any way but he does show it to her pastries and desserts, which might be why he proposes to her.<br /><br />Cath, feeling a disgusted pleasure, does not want to accept this proposal and marry the King. Luckily for her, on the same day, <b>a mysterious and new court joker who goes by the name of Jest,</b> arrives on the same day and steals a glance at Cath, not bothering to care about the interruption he just made. As Jest entered the ball and was able to talk to Cath in a way, the two start seeing each other more and all that leads to their own private courtship that is both loving but endangering to both, especially Cath.<br /><br />So to say it all, <b>I loved Heartless!</b> I really don't care what other have to say about this. I think I loved it so much because it was a retelling of the Queen of Hearts and not about Alice. What made me love this more was that Marissa included so many characters and aspects of the original retelling. We get the <b>Cheshire Cat, Jack 'The Knave of Hearts,' the Caterpillar, the White Rabbit, the Mad Hatter,</b> and other characters that were invented by Marissa. So I know <i>the Red Queen and the Queen of hearts</i> are different characters, but the White Queen and Red Queen were mentioned in this novel by Jest which was something that brought back memories from the movie as well. So to say it all, there were characters from the movie and the original Disney film. We also get such a different setting in this world. It's the world in Wonderland, but it was in the own creation and words of Marissa. It feels very different reading it when comparing it to the other films since it doesn't have to do much with Alice herself, but I was just glad Marissa was able to top that off as well. She was able to make this her own and unique world of Wonderland and it fit the characters and the story perfectly. Other kingdoms were mentioned as well and it was great finding out new things I actually didn't know about. The writing was also something I completely enjoyed! Like I said, Marissa has been the only author that has been able to captivate me into her new worlds and into her writing without complaints since the beginning. I'm always afraid to read retellings because I always think it will ruin the original fairy tale, but when it comes to Marissa, there's no doubt I'll love it.<br /><br />Cath was definitely a character I enjoyed reading about. She was a simple and normal girl who wanted to live a life she wanted to live, to choose the path she wanted to choose, not the ones her parents wanted for her. She was <b>good, understanding, lovely, adorable, and just</b> <i>cute!</i> It's a fantasy book, so I can't relate to characters, but Cath was a character I was able to understand from the beginning until the end. She had her own dreams and sometimes just wanted to run away and escape the world she was living in because she felt controlled at times by the King and her parents. She couldn't do everything she pleased or wanted to do, and she had to listen to everyone all the time and deal with it all. She didn't have many friends. In fact, she didn't have anyone to count on, not even Chesire. She couldn't trust herself to tell anyone anything or meet anyone knew and feel like they would become friends because she's never <b>had the heart to do that.</b> I sometimes felt bad for Cath and that is part of why I loved her character. She was just cute, that is all. She was also caring and nice but of course, the teenage girl must become the Queen of Hearts that orders to chop heads off and has everyone hating her.<br /><br />Another thing I loved about Cath is that she wasn't afraid to find out who this mysterious court joker and what he was up to, <b>Jest.</b> Jest was just wonderful in every way possible. He is another one of those fictional characters that are added to my book boyfriends list along with other girls and other book boyfriends over there who actually have a girlfriend ;) Jest was just the perfect one for Cath. I wouldn't call them boyfriend and girlfriend because their relationship actually started late, but the way their friendship was growing and turning into small aspects of a relationship was cute. Cath admitting to herself that she hated how she was falling for Jest immediately was funny, and of course, a book pet peeve of mine is insta love and I honestly hate it, but insta love here was different and I actually <b>didn't mind it</b> which is not something that usually happens. Never has happened, but with Heartless, history has been made. Cath and Jest both fell for each other and that involved insta love, but I wasn't upset. The only reason I hate it is because the author didn't write it correctly or in a way where I was able to enjoy it. There was no love triangle, and thank you, Marissa, for that, so instead love wasn't a problem. I loved them together since the beginning since Jest started his small performance that left the King and everyone else amazed and surprised and then just, <i>left.</i> Jest was just perfect. The ending doesn't change anything for me and I will love him forever and always. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Cath may be heartless but just like her, <b>I'm not heartless for Jest.</b> He's there in my heart and I thank him for coming into Cath's life and making it better. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> He brought her to different worlds. What I mean by that is that he was able to make Cath smile and laugh like no one else and I just loved that. Jest was just amazing in every way and I loved everything about him. He's a mysterious joker, a swoon-worthy male who had me giggling like a small 5-year-old fangirl because I couldn't get enough of him. Sana and I swooned over him since the beginning because he was a mysterious dude and he just sounded like those other attractive fictional characters. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>A joker. A rook. A mystery.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Unlike Jest and Cath, the other characters were the pieces of the book that I did not like in any way. Actually, I enjoyed the Raven and Chesire, but that's it. The King was very <b>immature, childish, a fool, and did not have any kind of ability to rule a kingdom.</b> He was a King who was very scared and did not have any protection under him in any way, he did not know how the care for a wife really is, and he couldn't do anything by himself. He and Cath were not meant to be together in any way and it's obvious from the start, which was another thing I was happy about. The other characters, like Jack and The Mad Hatter, were assholes at times as well. Jack, first, was the character I hated the most from the beginning besides the King. <b>He was a selfish guy who didn't care about anyone and anything besides himself and I really hated how he didn't try anything new.</b> The Mad Hatter was a little different than the Hatta we're familiar with. This guy created and gave hats that could turn people into someone else, which is found out as we learn a little more about him. <b>He was also mysterious, like the Joker, and he was also a selfish guy who didn't care much about the outside but only for himself and what he felt on the inside which was something I didn't like as well.</b> Even with the complaints I have with almost every other character, this book was just phenomenal! It was just what I needed; it was just the retelling I needed to read and I couldn't be happier to finally find a fairy tale retelling that made me my little red heart happy and then shattered it, not allowing it to feel anything. <br /><br />Marissa Meyer is just a wonderful writer and I'm so glad she was able to come up with this and write it the way I was expecting it. I'm really looking forward to her future novels, her upcoming releases, and anything she has in mind. I heard she's into fairy tales a lot so what she will normally write will be retellings and I am just perfectly okay with that. I loved this a lot, just a lot. I'm not in a hangover, but I feel many emotions towards that ending. <b>Those 4 last words, those 2 words that I read over and over again that made me sad over and over again when I knew that would happen.</b> I currently <b>hate</b> Sana for that because she kept telling me she had predictions and theories and me being the person that doesn't predict anything or have any theories because they can ruin the whole story for me, was very very mad at her. I don't ever predict (unless it's so obvious and it's like, right there) because sometimes I feel like I can or will be right and it will just ruin the whole thing for me. There won't be a point in reading the rest of the story if I already know what's gonna happen. Even if I spoiled myself, I would just skip to the end and say I finished it by skimming the last few pages or the rest of pages that were left of the book. I mean, that's happened a lot (when I spoil myself) so it wouldn't matter to me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12673763468886531446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer953689347031434617">DNF 53%<br/>I almost <i>never</i> give up on a book, but...<br/>Yikes. Um. Yeah, no.<br/>Sorry this one just <i>isn't</i> for me. I tried. But, it was just too boring for my personal taste.<br/>I should probably mention that I'm <b>not</b> an Alice in Wonderland fan. I've never read it, and I never plan to. In fact, I've never even made it all the way through the Disney movie. I know it's a classic and all, but even the animated version bores me.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441770954ra/16149272.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm not saying this story is boring, just that it's boring <i>
  <b>to me.</b>
</i> <br/>Catherine is the daug</span>
  <span id="freeText953689347031434617" style="display:none">DNF 53%<br>I almost <i>never</i> give up on a book, but...<br>Yikes. Um. Yeah, no.<br>Sorry this one just <i>isn't</i> for me. I tried. But, it was just too boring for my personal taste.<br>I should probably mention that I'm <b>not</b> an Alice in Wonderland fan. I've never read it, and I never plan to. In fact, I've never even made it all the way through the Disney movie. I know it's a classic and all, but even the animated version bores me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441770954ra/16149272.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm not saying this story is boring, just that it's boring <i>
  <b>to me.</b>
</i> <br>Catherine is the daughter of a marquess, but wants to be a baker. She's getting pushed into marrying the King of Heart, but she's in love with the Jester. In the background, there's a monster (Jabberwocky) on the loose. And there's all sorts of Alice in Wonderland characters/references going on throughout. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486494430ra/21920600.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And since I'm in the very small minority, I'm assuming that all of the above mentioned stuff was wonderful for most of the readers. To me though, it was chock full of equal parts weird and dull. The world's most snoozworthy romance happening in Trippyville.<br>I've been struggling with this book for over a month now, and I finally decided to take the coward's way out, and <i>*GASP!*</i> skip to the last few pages to see how it all turned out.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478993365ra/21137701.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah, no thanks.<br>I've only DNF'd a small handful of books over the years, but I'm afraid this is going to have to be one of them. I could lie to myself and say <i>maybe I'll come back to it at a later date</i>, but you and I both know that ain't happening. Due to all the glowing reviews, I don't think most of you will find this book as unreadable as I did, so take my opinion with a grain of salt.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486741047ra/21946006.gif" width="35400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1289097912" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1289097912" />
    <a title="P " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25327841-p"><img alt="P " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489853536p2/25327841.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1289097912?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="P " class="user" itemprop="url" name="P " href="/user/show/25327841-p">P </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25327841-p?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1289097912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12760334452776441232"><b>
  <blockquote>“Roses are red, violets are blue,<br/>I would even trim my moustache for you!” </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484214315i/21694150._SY540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book is magic. I could feel it everywhere when words were recounted, when songs were chanted and when hearts were broken. Other than that, the book made me giggle continually. Catherine has the great development since the beginning. Her character is played out an exact direction as a good girl constrained by traditions. And then she meets Jest, her heart is conveyed out of the path of marrying the King of Hearts. </span>
  <span id="freeText12760334452776441232" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“Roses are red, violets are blue,<br>I would even trim my moustache for you!” </blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484214315i/21694150._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is magic. I could feel it everywhere when words were recounted, when songs were chanted and when hearts were broken. Other than that, the book made me giggle continually. Catherine has the great development since the beginning. Her character is played out an exact direction as a good girl constrained by traditions. And then she meets Jest, her heart is conveyed out of the path of marrying the King of Hearts. Cath was my main focus through this book. I admired her at first, but around the middle I felt as if her personality was queerly changed. I should have felt good with it, but I didn't. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“When pleased, I beat like a drum. When sad, I break like glass. Once stolen, I can never be taken back. What am I?”</blockquote>
</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484214315ra/21694151.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There was something about Heartless making me quaver all the time. I was afraid that this book would be another <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22489107.Fairest__The_Lunar_Chronicles___3_5_" title="Fairest (The Lunar Chronicles, #3.5) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Fairest</a>, a pitiful girl turns villainous by people around her. Anyhow, the ending was not what I was afraid of, and I was quite satisfied with those twists and turns flipping my stomach and wrenching my heart painfully. I kinda understood the motivations of the MCs, though. They follows the story that already happened in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13023.Alice_in_Wonderland__Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland___1_" title="Alice in Wonderland (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland, #1) by Lewis Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice in Wonderland</a>, which Marissa Meyer tried so hard to respect the original one, and she did well.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Over everything, I choose you”</blockquote>
</b> <br><br>Apart from my rumbling stomach, I have some problems with Heartless, too, for its lack of dymanic throughout the story. The narration is good but slow, and if someone doesn't enjoy the courtesy of the Victorian era as I did, it'll be boring and easy to lose interest since the first few chapters. By the by, I liked many things of Heartless: its characters, story, twists and magical world which divided by the Looking Glass. They captured my atttention successfully and made me fall in love with Alice in Wonderland all over again.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423711391ra/13661892.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432742411ra/15003366.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Why is a raven like a writing-desk?”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>One final question.<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://goo.gl/eMCgl4">https://goo.gl/eMCgl4</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12760334452776441232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1290072808" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1290072808" />
    <a title="Joelle (Throne of books) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17660097-joelle-throne-of-books"><img alt="Joelle (Throne of books) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587611161p2/17660097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1290072808?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joelle (Throne of books) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joelle (Throne of books) " href="/user/show/17660097-joelle-throne-of-books">Joelle (Throne of books) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17660097-joelle-throne-of-books?shelf=arc-reviews">arc-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1290072808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13166731336641506450">   *3.5 stars* <br/> Heartless by Marissa Meyer is an Alice in Wonderland prequel set long before the infamous Queen of Hearts was the terror of Wonderland. Back when she was just a girl who wanted to fall in love.<br/><br/>  While being one of the most beautiful girls in wonderland and a favorite of the King of Hearts, as a talented baker all Catherine wants is to open a bakery with her best friend.  Unfortunately, her parents such a dream is absurd for someone who could be the next queen. <br/>  Not reciprocating</span>
  <span id="freeText13166731336641506450" style="display:none">   *3.5 stars* <br /> Heartless by Marissa Meyer is an Alice in Wonderland prequel set long before the infamous Queen of Hearts was the terror of Wonderland. Back when she was just a girl who wanted to fall in love.<br /><br />  While being one of the most beautiful girls in wonderland and a favorite of the King of Hearts, as a talented baker all Catherine wants is to open a bakery with her best friend.  Unfortunately, her parents such a dream is absurd for someone who could be the next queen. <br />  Not reciprocating the Kings feelings for her, Catherine meets the mysterious yet handsome court joker, Jest, at the royal ball where the kind is to propose to her. Determined to define her destiny and fall in love on her own terms, she and Jest enter a secret courtship. <br /><br />  The first thing I want to clarify as most people seem to be confused on the matter, is that the Queen of Hearts and the Red Queen are not the same person. People often confuse the two but alas they are not the same. They're both evil Queens yes, but originally the queen of hearts was first introduced in Lewis Carroll's  'Alice's adventures in wonderland' the  Red Queen was introduced in 'Alice through the looking Glass' I do believe all this confusion is due to the mispresentation of them in Tim Burton's popular movie adaptation. <br /><br /><br /><br />  That being said I want to thank Marissa Meyer for writing such a wonderful origin story to one of my favorite villains of all time. I am a HUGE fan of Alice in Wonderland. And I am an even bigger fan of villains. Getting to read Marissa's version of the Queen of Hearts' evil origin was incredible. <br /><br />  Catherine was on many levels, one of the most relatable characters I've ever read about. All she wants is to open up a bakery with her best friend Mary Anne. Baking pastries and delicacies is where her heart belongs. However, her parents want her to seize such silly dreams and focus on other appropriate acts for young ladies such as herself. That includes marrying the King of Hearts. Even though that is not what she wants, Catherine wants her parents disappointment even less. Catherine's parents are infuriating people. Not once do they stop to ask her if she is happy. Not once do they stop and consider that this might not be what she wants. Her mother, is biggest nightmare of them all. Refusing to speak of anything other than her future wedding and queenly status, she hurts Catherine with her words. She often chastised her for eating too much or even considering having another bite. Comparing her to a hefty animal. <br /><br />  Jest, the mysterious new court joker makes her feel -for the first time- what love really is. He is mysterious, handsome and captivating. She feels gers left drawn to him from the minute she first sees him, and something inside her starts to bloom. <br />   The romance between the two was something that stubbornly latched onto my heart and refused to let go until the very end when it consumed my heart entirely. <br />I tried not to get hopeful considering we all know how the Queen of Hearts ends up but try as I might, it was impossible. <br /><br />  The plot of the story is well  known of course. Unfortunately the pacing was relatively slow for the majority of the book. However, as soon as I began the luscious writing pulled me into the story and I couldn't put the book down. I was drawn in completely. One thing Marissa can really do is write compellingly. <br /><br />   While I can't discuss much else without spoiling the anything I do want to say that I was CRUSHED by the end. Heartless is such a good title for this book because that is exactly (not really!) what Marissa Meyer is for ruining me the way she did. I'm convinced she should write an Alice in Wonderland retelling because you have to admit, the woman can write one hell of a retelling. And of course, a villains' beautifully tragic origin story. <br /><br />  And the moment everyone's being waiting for (let's be honest here you're all waiting for it) the comparison to The Lunar chronicles. Yes, I know many of you want to know if it's better than her Lunar chronicles series and I'll get right to the point. It's not. In my opinion, it was not. The Lunar chronicles is a far better series and story. While heartless was very enjoyable, it was very slow paced and than RUSHED in the end. Of course, I believe this is due to the fact that it is a standalone. If it had been the beginning of a new series I don't doubt it would have been better paced and plotted out. I do still recommend you give this story a shot if you're a fan of Alice in Wonderland such as myself or if you love Meyers' other works.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13166731336641506450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2176917540" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9432732179975351502"><i> “These things do not happen in dreams, dear girl,’ he said, vanishing up to his neck. ‘They happen only in nightmares.’ </i><br/><br/>This was great! In the beginning, I wasn’t sure - it was rather cutesy, and I found Cath slightly irritating. <br/>But as I carried on, this book grew darker and darker! I loved being immersed in Meyer’s version of Wonderland, with many characters to be recognised; including the Caterpillar, the White Rabbit, the Hatter, March Hare, Doormouse, Cheshire Cat and even Mary-Ann for any</span>
  <span id="freeText9432732179975351502" style="display:none"><i> “These things do not happen in dreams, dear girl,’ he said, vanishing up to his neck. ‘They happen only in nightmares.’ </i><br /><br />This was great! In the beginning, I wasn’t sure - it was rather cutesy, and I found Cath slightly irritating. <br />But as I carried on, this book grew darker and darker! I loved being immersed in Meyer’s version of Wonderland, with many characters to be recognised; including the Caterpillar, the White Rabbit, the Hatter, March Hare, Doormouse, Cheshire Cat and even Mary-Ann for any super fans of the Disney film. <br />Cath is the daughter of the Marquess of Turtle Rock Cove and a shoe in to become the King of Hearts’ future bride. Unfortunately, she has no desire to be Queen of the Kingdom of Hearts. She’d much rather set up a Bakery business with her best friend Mary-Ann and do something she loves. <br />At one of the King’s numerous parties, Cath fears an imminent proposal and flees into the castle gardens, where she meets the Court Joker - Jest. He is witty, clever and with a knack for the impossible. <br />Suddenly Cath finds herself even more desperate than before to avoid engagement to the King. <br />Throw in battles with the Jabberwock and mysterious items coming over from the land of Chess; entered only through the looking glass and a well watched over by three creepy girls and this book has some serious fantasticalness! <br />But as we all know how the story ends, it was frightening to see how everything would unravel, and there was so much magic and world building, I was both enraptured and heart broken all at the same time! <br />4 stars 🌟</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1787100167" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1787100167" />
    <a title="Aneela ♒the_mystique_reader♒" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29923106-aneela-the-mystique-reader"><img alt="Aneela ♒the_mystique_reader♒" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487600612p2/29923106.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1787100167?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aneela ♒the_mystique_reader♒" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aneela ♒the_mystique_reader♒" href="/user/show/29923106-aneela-the-mystique-reader">Aneela ♒the_mystique_reader♒</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29923106-aneela-the-mystique-reader?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29923106-aneela-the-mystique-reader?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29923106-aneela-the-mystique-reader?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29923106-aneela-the-mystique-reader?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29923106-aneela-the-mystique-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1787100167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10808674316296882702"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500824856i/23387562._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>My Rating:</u>
</b><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500432857i/23338720._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/> <br/><b>
  <u>Synopsis:</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>“It was impossible, and she absolutely believed it.”</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>Catherine Pinkerton lives in Hearts. She is the only daughter of Marquess and Marchioness. King of Hearts fancies her to be his wife and Queen of Hearts. But Catherine has other plans. The throne of Hearts does not appeal her. She is a baker at heart and has a dream of opening her own bakery where she could make delectables that no one has ever tasted. But that is not the only thing she dreams about.<br/><br/>Both her dre</span>
  <span id="freeText10808674316296882702" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500824856i/23387562._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>
  <u>My Rating:</u>
</b><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500432857i/23338720._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <br><b>
  <u>Synopsis:</u>
</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“It was impossible, and she absolutely believed it.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Catherine Pinkerton lives in Hearts. She is the only daughter of Marquess and Marchioness. King of Hearts fancies her to be his wife and Queen of Hearts. But Catherine has other plans. The throne of Hearts does not appeal her. She is a baker at heart and has a dream of opening her own bakery where she could make delectables that no one has ever tasted. But that is not the only thing she dreams about.<br><br>Both her dreams can lead her astray from a reputable life. She could either choose to follow her dreams or be a part of gentry she despise.<br><br>But is the choice really hers to make???<br><br> <br><b>
  <u>Review:</u>
</b><br><br>Heartless is inspired by Alice in Wonderland by Lewis Carroll. This is not a retelling, to be precise. Though the novel is set in the same magical place of talking animals and other mythical creatures. It is like Marissa Meyer borrowed some characters from Alice in Wonderland and spun a new fantasy novel around them.<br><br>And I found this novel to be very enchanting except for the first 40 percent where we are told about Catherine’s bakery dream and her struggles to avoid King’s proposal, numerous times. Not only that, it was too irritating to read again and again about how much the Marchioness wants Catherine to marry the King. Trust me, every time the Marchioness asks Catherine if the King has proposed her or not I was like why not she herself marries the King. She was so desperate that it all started to get boring and I was wondering if I want to further read the book or not. I am glad I did read it.<br><br>The rest 60 percent was just too good and I loved the twists and turns in the latter 60% of the book. I did not want this book to end. The main reason was Jest. I was so in love with this character. He is truly unforgettable.<br><br> <br><br><b>
  <u>Why I loved this Book:</u>
</b><br><br><b>1. Jest</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Impossible was his speciality.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Once in a while we come across such a character that appeals us most. We want to read that book again just because of that character. Jest is that character for me in the book. He is funny, smart and handsome. A character beautifully written and would be engraved in the memory of the readers for a very very long time.<br><br>2. <b>Hatta</b><br><br>Hatta is the same mad hatter of the Alice in Wonderland. He crafts wonderful hats. Reading about him created the image of Johnny Depp playing Mad Hatter from the movie in my mind.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1485862503ra/21855132.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After Jest, Hatta is my second most favorite character of the book. His weird sense of humor, sarcastic remarks and selfless nature make him unique.<br><br>3. <b>The Three Sisters</b><br><br>Since I don’t want to give away any spoilers, I would only say the Three Sisters were the most crepiest, scariest and weirdest characters of the book and yet I loved them. Ironic, isn’t it?<br><br>4. <b>The Chemistry and Spark Between Catherine and Jest:</b><br><br>They just click! You know the feeling of reading about lovers who are made for each other. The feels they give you.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“She felt like she could talk to him for hours, for days and months and years, and never tire of it.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>It feels like you are there sharing their beautiful moments with them.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>She started to shake her head, to be firm in her stance that this, whatever this was, could not continue past this night, this morning, this very moment. ‘Jest . . .’<br>His eyebrows lifted and he looked pleased at the intimacy of his name.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Oh my God! It tickled my heart and tummy when I read the dialogues between the two.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I thought I could take a walk, look around. I’m still new to these parts.’<br>‘But you’re not walking. You’re climbing trees.’<br>‘It’s still exercise.’</blockquote>
</b><br><br><br>The way he confesses his love to her:<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>‘Catherine, I don’t want your heart to belong to anyone but me.’</blockquote>
</b><br><br>How he makes her smile and laugh:<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>He looked up at her and smiled that disarming smile again. ‘I’m a joker, my lady, which is even better.’<br>‘How is that better than a doctor?’<br>‘Haven’t you ever heard that laughter is the best medicine?’</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>5. Catherine’s Dreams:</b><br><br>Just read the following lines from the book:<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Hundreds and hundreds of small, delicate hearts surrounded her – all of them bleeding.<br>She reached up and touched a finger to the soft flesh of the nearest bud, gathering a single drop of warm blood on her fingertip. Each bleeding heart bloom was a delicate thing, beautiful and haunting.<br>She crushed the flower in her fist, relishing the wet smear in her palm.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Needless I say anything. Her dreams were magical!<br><br><b>
  <u>What I didn’t like:</u>
</b><br><br><b>1. Catherine</b><br><br>To be honest, I did not like Catherine at all. She was selfish and a hypocrite. The only good quality she has was her baking skills.<br><br><b>2. The Marchioness and her desperation towards King:</b><br><br>She was the most irritating character of the book. If she could, she would have forced Catherine to marry the King on gunpoint or canon-point.<br><br> <br><br><b>
  <u>Conclucion:</u>
</b><br>I wanted to give this book 4 stars instead of 5 because of slower 40% part of the book. But I couldn’t. The fast paced 60% of the book was so full of twists and turns that were worthy of 5 stars. Plus Jest himself deserves 5 stars. What a marvelous character! What an amazing book!<br><br><a href="https://themystiquereader.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10808674316296882702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
